# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api`, `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd`

# Kubernetes Scheduler Plugin Framework Architecture

## Your Task

A new Kubernetes contributor wants to understand the scheduler plugin framework architecture. Find the key Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the scheduling framework: 1. The framework interface definitions (Plugin, FilterPlugin, ScorePlugin, BindPlugin, etc. in pkg/scheduler/framework/). 2. The ScheduleOne orchestration function that drives the scheduling cycle for a single pod. 3. The top-level Scheduler struct and its Run method. 4. The frameworkImpl runtime that invokes plugins (RunFilterPlugins, RunScorePlugins). 5. The plugin registry and the NewInTreeRegistry that registers all built-in plugins. Report each file path and key symbols.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the onboarding domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've successfully analyzed the Kubernetes scheduler plugin framework architecture and created a comprehensive report. Here's what I found:

## Summary of Key Findings

I've documented **6 core files** that implement the scheduler plugin framework:

1. **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** - Contains all plugin interface definitions:
   - Base `Plugin` interface
   - 11 specialized plugin types: `PreEnqueuePlugin`, `QueueSortPlugin`, `PreFilterPlugin`, `FilterPlugin`, `PostFilterPlugin`, `PreScorePlugin`, `ScorePlugin`, `ReservePlugin`, `PreBindPlugin`, `PostBindPlugin`, `PermitPlugin`, `BindPlugin`
   - The main `Framework` interface that aggregates all plugin functionality

2. **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** - The `ScheduleOne()` function orchestrates the complete scheduling workflow for a single pod

3. **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** - The top-level `Scheduler` struct and its `Run()` method that manages the overall scheduler lifecycle

4. **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** - The `frameworkImpl` runtime that:
   - Implements the `Framework` interface
   - Provides `RunFilterPlugins()` and `RunScorePlugins()` methods
   - Manages plugin lifecycle and execution

5. **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go** - Defines the `Registry` type that stores plugin factories

6. **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/registry.go** - Contains `NewInTreeRegistry()` that registers all 17+ built-in plugins

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed information about files, symbols, the execution chain, and a narrative explanation of the architecture.

These plugins are\\n652: \\t// informational. A common application of this extension point is for cleaning\\n653: \\t// up. Permit\\n663: \\t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\\n664: \\t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\\n665: \\t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\\n666: \\t// waiting. Bind\\n672: // plugins are used to bind a pod to a Node.\\n673: type BindPlugin interface {\\n674: \\tPlugin\\n675: \\t// Bind plugins will not be called until all pre-bind plugins have completed. The main plugin interfaces are:\\n- PreEnqueuePlugin: Called before pods are added to the active queue\\n- QueueSortPlugin: Sorts pods in the scheduling queue (only one enabled at a time)\\n- EnqueueExtensions: Optional interface for efficient pod movement in scheduling queues\\n- PreFilterPlugin: Called at the beginning of a scheduling cycle; can return PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate\\n- FilterPlugin: Filters out hosts that cannot run a pod (formerly called 'predicates')\\n- PostFilterPlugin: Called after a pod cannot be scheduled; used for preemption logic\\n- PreScorePlugin: Informational extension point after filtering; plugins can update internal state\\n- ScorePlugin: Ranks nodes that passed the filtering phase; must implement Score() and optionally ScoreExtensions() with NormalizeScore()\\n- ReservePlugin: Updates plugin state when scheduler cache is updated; has Reserve() and Unreserve() methods\\n- PreBindPlugin: Called before a pod is bound to a node\\n- BindPlugin: Binds a pod to a node (at most one BindPlugin handles the binding)\\n- PostBindPlugin: Called after a pod is successfully bound; used for cleanup\\n- PermitPlugin: Called before binding; can prevent or delay pod binding\\n\\nAll plugins implement the Plugin interface which requires a Name() method. The Framework interface is the main contract that aggregates all plugin-related functionality.\\n\\n**2. ScheduleOne Orchestration (pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go):**\\nThe ScheduleOne() function (line 65) is the main entry point that orchestrates the scheduling workflow for a single pod. It:\\n- Gets the next pod from the scheduling queue via NextPod()\\n- Retrieves the appropriate framework for the pod\\n- Creates a fresh CycleState for the scheduling cycle\\n- Calls schedulingCycle() which invokes the scheduling plugins in sequence\\n- On success, asynchronously calls bindingCycle() to bind the pod\\n\\n**3. Top-Level Scheduler Struct (pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go):**\\nThe Scheduler struct (line 66) is the main component that watches for new unscheduled pods and attempts to find suitable nodes. The Run() method (line 464) starts the scheduler in a goroutine, initializing the scheduling queue and the scheduleOne loop.\\n\\n**4. FrameworkImpl Runtime (pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go):**\\nThe frameworkImpl struct (line 52) is responsible for initializing and running scheduler plugins. Key methods include:\\n- RunPreFilterPlugins() (line 697): Runs PreFilter plugins; returns PreFilterResult and status\\n- RunFilterPlugins() (line 872): Runs Filter plugins; returns status for each node\\n- RunPostFilterPlugins() (line 919): Runs PostFilter plugins for preemption\\n- RunPreScorePlugins() (line 1075): Runs PreScore plugins\\n- RunScorePlugins() (line 1112): Runs Score plugins in parallel and handles score normalization\\nThe frameworkImpl maintains lists of all configured plugins for each extension point and orchestrates their execution with proper error handling and metrics recording.\\n\\n**5. Plugin Registry (pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go and pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/registry.go):**\\nThe Registry type (line 71 in registry.go) is a map[string]PluginFactory that holds all available plugins. The NewInTreeRegistry() function (pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/registry.go, line 47) builds the registry with all in-tree plugins including:\\n- DynamicResources, ImageLocality, TaintToleration, NodeName, NodePorts\\n- NodeAffinity, PodTopologySpread, NodeUnschedulable, NodeResources\\n- VolumeBinding, VolumeRestrictions, VolumeZone, NodeVolumeLimits\\n- InterPodAffinity, QueueSort, DefaultBinder, DefaultPreemption, SchedulingGates\\n\\nThe Registry supports Register(), Unregister(), and Merge() operations. Out-of-tree plugins can be registered via the WithFrameworkOutOfTreeRegistry option when building the scheduler.\\n\\nThe complete scheduling pipeline flows: Scheduler.Run() \u2192 ScheduleOne() \u2192 schedulingCycle() \u2192 RunPreFilterPlugins() \u2192 RunFilterPlugins() \u2192 RunScorePlugins() \u2192 bindingCycle() with various other plugins invoked at appropriate extension points throughout the cycle.\"\n}\n",
